    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer7781325010505338062"><strong>The debut novel from award-winning filmmaker Rohith S. Katbamna, tells the powerful story of a brave few who venture for truth in the aftermath of a global uprising.</strong><br/><br/>In the year 2027, society has fallen. Mass revolts and warring nations have claimed countless lives and destroyed vast lands. Forced into a dark slumber, the world now draws fewer breaths and hosts infinite gra</span>
  <span id="freeText7781325010505338062" style="display:none"><strong>The debut novel from award-winning filmmaker Rohith S. Katbamna, tells the powerful story of a brave few who venture for truth in the aftermath of a global uprising.</strong><br /><br />In the year 2027, society has fallen. Mass revolts and warring nations have claimed countless lives and destroyed vast lands. Forced into a dark slumber, the world now draws fewer breaths and hosts infinite graveyards.<br /><br />In England, ten survivors who have journeyed many miles are on a path ready to converge. With histories soaked in the blood of betrayal, lies and deceit, one common thread binds them. The human instinct to seek a greater truth.<br /><br />Over six days, these ten souls will come to find that the ruined world around them is reawakening. As a presence emerges, bringing with it a merciless intention to eliminate any and all beating bodies, this company of strangers will confront a series of hardships in a tale of underdogs, oppressors and the human condition.<br /><br /><em><strong>Down and Rising</strong> is an immersive reading experience. An imaginative multi-story arc intricately woven together by striking imagery, reference materials and finely crafted characters.</em></span>
  <a data-text-id="7781325010505338062" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2650107756" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2650107756" />
    <a title="Raymond Chou" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/91455198-raymond-chou"><img alt="Raymond Chou" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598445343p2/91455198.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2650107756?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Raymond Chou" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Raymond Chou" href="/user/show/91455198-raymond-chou">Raymond Chou</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2650107756" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12108563780024548145"><b>*I was fortunate to read an advanced copy as part of an impartial reader's circle before buying a copy upon release.</b><br/><br/><i>Cover Art:</i> A canvas style painting with the duplicate image of a girl’s face. In addition, 10 flowers that if left to my interpretation, represent the 10 main characters. What makes this cover that much more important, is how it has been woven into the fabric of the story. You learn from the beginning that everything in this book has a reason for its place.<br/><br/><i>Characters:</i> I was apprehe</span>
  <span id="freeText12108563780024548145" style="display:none"><b>*I was fortunate to read an advanced copy as part of an impartial reader's circle before buying a copy upon release.</b><br /><br /><i>Cover Art:</i> A canvas style painting with the duplicate image of a girl’s face. In addition, 10 flowers that if left to my interpretation, represent the 10 main characters. What makes this cover that much more important, is how it has been woven into the fabric of the story. You learn from the beginning that everything in this book has a reason for its place.<br /><br /><i>Characters:</i> I was apprehensive about seeing an ensemble collection of characters because I mainly found my most enjoyable reading experiences to be those that focused on 2 or 3 key people. However, in ‘Down and Rising’, the author managed to pull off what I feel is rare these days. Rounded out characters, whom I cared for, warts and all.<br /><br /><i>Story:</i> I came in expecting zombies, nuclear mutations and all of the other tropes we have grown accustomed to with post-apocalyptic tales. This shelves all those in favour of the human story. A unique focus on social and political culture that funnily enough mirrors in many ways today’s situation. I found myself smiling at points because where we are now doesn’t seem too far off (in some ways) from where 2027 is in ‘Down and Rising’.<br /><br />The story was told in a very cinematic sense. Heavy on the psychological drama and suspense and just as much on the violence and action - all the while with a grounded control of realism.<br /><br />The reveals, the twists, the turns - are sewn beautifully throughout for a page-turning experience. <br /><br />Structure: This is perhaps one of the easiest parts to highlight. Not only are we greeted with flashback storytelling through a main liner arc, but we are offered reading materials between chapters. Each offering supplemental and interesting knowledge while continuing to world-build. We see background information on certain characters and storylines and clues and nuggets to events that are to come later in the story. <br /><br />Conclusion: Patience. This book is about patience. Taking the time to understand each other. Our world isn't moving fast. Our perception is. A very enlightening read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12108563780024548145" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15888648434007265643">WARNING: This book is suitable for mature readers.<br/><br/>There is violence, strong language, disturbing events.<br/><br/>REVIEW: Down and Rising made me feel optimistic in a strange way. Considering how depressing the situation of the 'end of the world' appeared in this story, the hopeful glimmers and strong messaging on never giving up no matter what, shone through.<br/><br/>There is so much to take from this story and I can't really compile them into a single review. But I will say this. I feel informed and alert to thi</span>
  <span id="freeText15888648434007265643" style="display:none">WARNING: This book is suitable for mature readers.<br /><br />There is violence, strong language, disturbing events.<br /><br />REVIEW: Down and Rising made me feel optimistic in a strange way. Considering how depressing the situation of the 'end of the world' appeared in this story, the hopeful glimmers and strong messaging on never giving up no matter what, shone through.<br /><br />There is so much to take from this story and I can't really compile them into a single review. But I will say this. I feel informed and alert to things in my life that I wasn't necessarily aware of before. Whether it's information consumption or human decency, these things were strongly represented in Down and Rising.<br /><br />As for why one should read this book, or who should read this book... I'd say anyone who wants to be challenged or is open to being challenged on their views and judgements. It's a book on the human condition and in some ways, the psychological make-up of society. <br /><br />A final note - creative approach to presenting literary fiction through artistic images. Wonderful work by Filmon Belay.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2660589907" />
    <a title="Yasmin Khan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/91739650-yasmin-khan"><img alt="Yasmin Khan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565783503p2/91739650.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Yasmin Khan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Yasmin Khan" href="/user/show/91739650-yasmin-khan">Yasmin Khan</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2660589907" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5412091131882927156">Had the chance to read this back in November as part of a reader's circle.<br/><br/>For a debut book, it certainly didn't read like one from a first-time novelist. <br/><br/>Down and Rising has been written with punch and confidence. A relevant tale set in the near future but in many ways is unfolding before our very eyes.<br/><br/>Considering the story is set over 6 days, it feels like an epic novel. We dive into character's lives in both the past and the present and are gifted with rich 'historical materials' to feed the r</span>
  <span id="freeText5412091131882927156" style="display:none">Had the chance to read this back in November as part of a reader's circle.<br /><br />For a debut book, it certainly didn't read like one from a first-time novelist. <br /><br />Down and Rising has been written with punch and confidence. A relevant tale set in the near future but in many ways is unfolding before our very eyes.<br /><br />Considering the story is set over 6 days, it feels like an epic novel. We dive into character's lives in both the past and the present and are gifted with rich 'historical materials' to feed the reader experience.<br /><br />There is a nice touch with blank pages between chapters titled 'Readers Notes'. I found this to be an additional effort on immersing me even more into the story. It also helped me to reflect on what I had just read, especially after coming back to pick up where I'd left off.<br /><br />A wonderful read and easily one of the most striking pieces of literature I have read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5412091131882927156" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5263215505886170712">Went in cold. Came out burning.<br/><br/>The 'Salvage Entries' segment is an excellent addition to the end of a 6 day odyssey of blood, sweat and tears.<br/><br/>For someone who finds themselves distancing from the media and barrage of bias news etc. Down and Rising is a truly sobering read. It doesn't side completely with one or the other when it comes to politics. It takes a common sense and logical approach insisting on being fundamentally sound.   <span id="freeText5263215505886170712" style="display:none">Went in cold. Came out burning.<br /><br />The 'Salvage Entries' segment is an excellent addition to the end of a 6 day odyssey of blood, sweat and tears.<br /><br />For someone who finds themselves distancing from the media and barrage of bias news etc. Down and Rising is a truly sobering read. Using simple approaches for complex situations.<br /><br />We get too tied up in trying to be 'smart' that we get blinded by the solution that's in front of our face.<br /><br />Powerful and brutal. Will be re-reading because there was so much in this and I have a feeling the experience will alter each time I read it while I come to understand certain aspects.</span>

<div id="review_2697962460" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2697962460" />
    <a title="Danica Matus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/92977223-danica-matus"><img alt="Danica Matus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552127532p2/92977223.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2697962460?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Danica Matus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Danica Matus" href="/user/show/92977223-danica-matus">Danica Matus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/92977223-danica-matus?shelf=post-apocalyptic">post-apocalyptic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2697962460" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7022153088637119908">Imaginative. Striking. Visceral. Un-filtered. <br/><br/>Firstly, don't take this book on the subway. It's heavy and unless you've big hands, it'll be uncomfortable. It's a book made for someone who has put some time aside or will be in one place and not on the move. Patience is a virtue.<br/><br/>Secondly, the artwork is fab! It's designed as if the artist has literally drawn on the paper itself and gives that authentic/classical feel.<br/><br/>Thirdly, the story is one of the most layered and fleshed out narratives I've had</span>
  <span id="freeText7022153088637119908" style="display:none">Imaginative. Striking. Visceral. Un-filtered. <br /><br />Firstly, don't take this book on the subway. It's heavy and unless you've big hands, it'll be uncomfortable. It's a book made for someone who has put some time aside or will be in one place and not on the move. Patience is a virtue.<br /><br />Secondly, the artwork is fab! It's designed as if the artist has literally drawn on the paper itself and gives that authentic/classical feel.<br /><br />Thirdly, the story is one of the most layered and fleshed out narratives I've had the pleasure of reading. I was and still am invested. I want more. I want to see where it goes or can go because there is a world here to explore and plunder for more creative riches.<br /><br />This is most certainly a psychological odyssey of epic proportions. A creative feat that leaves you humbled and fulfilled - yet you want more!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7022153088637119908" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2730748471" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2730748471" />
    <a title="James Herring" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/94127772-james-herring"><img alt="James Herring" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2730748471?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James Herring" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James Herring" href="/user/show/94127772-james-herring">James Herring</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/94127772-james-herring?shelf=essential-reading">essential-reading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/94127772-james-herring?shelf=hybrid">hybrid</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/94127772-james-herring?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2730748471" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16660837107446074478">There have only been a handful of books in my life which I have deemed as true page-turners. This is undoubtedly one of those books.<br/><br/>Let's start with the plot: the year is 2027 and the 'world has fallen'. Doom and gloom befalls the broken landscapes and its characters. Something even more rotten lies underneath. This isn't just a story about 10 or so people uniting for a common truth. It's about home truths. Personal truths. The dark and seedy. The light and hopeful. There is pain and great strug</span>
  <span id="freeText16660837107446074478" style="display:none">There have only been a handful of books in my life which I have deemed as true page-turners. This is undoubtedly one of those books.<br /><br />Let's start with the plot: the year is 2027 and the 'world has fallen'. Doom and gloom befalls the broken landscapes and its characters. Something even more rotten lies underneath. This isn't just a story about 10 or so people uniting for a common truth. It's about home truths. Personal truths. The dark and seedy. The light and hopeful. There is pain and great struggle. A cacophony of themes not only for those in the story but for the reader. For me. For you. For our society.<br /><br />The presentation/structure: a creative recipe of life-like newspaper cuttings, radio interviews, photographs and other interesting academic-like resource features. They're all tantamount to the story. A narrative builder. Thickening the substance and making for a pleasurable and often addictive read.<br /><br />The message: change is frightening but necessary. Problems are complicated but solvable. Society is abrassive but compassion and empathy are the elixir.<br /><br /><b>"True deliverance is the liberation of the mind and the embrace of human compassion."</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="16660837107446074478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2447310653160947741">This was a hard read at times because of the subject matter. It was hardhitting and didn't hold back.<br/><br/>As someone who has gone through much of a particular character in this book (won't mention which one), I felt like I was reading an auto-biography at moments. The detail was grand and the visual scape painted through the words and description was fantastic. I don't think I've ever read a book that has made me feel so overcome with emotion. The connections between these characters and the ideas of</span>
  <span id="freeText2447310653160947741" style="display:none">This was a hard read at times because of the subject matter. It was hardhitting and didn't hold back.<br /><br />As someone who has gone through much of a particular character in this book (won't mention which one), I felt like I was reading an auto-biography at moments. The detail was grand and the visual scape painted through the words and description was fantastic. I don't think I've ever read a book that has made me feel so overcome with emotion. The connections between these characters and the ideas of loyalty and compassion were so welcomed. The story was next level, in my opinion. Political games played at the highest level through manipulation and deception. A strange education that feels familiar when you look online or hear on the radio. Really hits home.<br /><br />I don't feel there is such a thing as an original idea these days, but there is an original voice telling an original take in an original way when it comes to Down and Rising. A must-read. I'm sure I will read it again later in the year.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9094039896721754069">My first question was something like, "is this another 'sh*t on the world' book?"<br/><br/>This was before I read DOWN AND RISING.<br/><br/>My answer was firmly given by the end of the first chapter. It wasn't about sh*tting on the world. Nor was it about nihilism or misanthropy. Popular hipster things to do or be these days.   <span id="freeText9094039896721754069" style="display:none">My first question was something like, "is this another 'sh*t on the world' book?"<br /><br />This was before I read DOWN AND RISING.<br /><br />My answer was firmly given by the end of the first chapter. It wasn't about sh*tting on the world. Nor was it about nihilism or misanthropy. Popular hipster things to do or be these days. It was about widening your perspective and looking at the world as a community. An extended family. Being open-minded and giving and sometimes the downsides to these - but how not to be dissuaded by the 'few' bad things that can happen. <br /><br />I think we tend to focus on the one negative among the 99 positives. Might be the human make-up, our ego and so on. All I know is that I feel encouraged to focus more on the latter. The positives. This is progression - and that's what DOWN AND RISING was for me. The goal of progressing as a human society. <br /><br />Proves that even in the fiercest brutality, you can still lift yourself and others up.</span>

    <a title="Sam Larson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/93565229-sam-larson"><img alt="Sam Larson" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2715099207?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam Larson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam Larson" href="/user/show/93565229-sam-larson">Sam Larson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/93565229-sam-larson?shelf=essential-reading">essential-reading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/93565229-sam-larson?shelf=post-apocalyptic">post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/93565229-sam-larson?shelf=underrated">underrated</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2715099207" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18211880477717291749">It was the characters that did it for me.<br/><br/>Even though the story was pretty damn brilliant, the characters (who felt like real-life people) were absorbing and moving. I actually can't remember the last time I felt this attached to literary characters.<br/><br/>Arav and Jared are complete standouts. The latter will probably be the most controversial and most complex. But go in with an open mind and try to put your personal bias and pre-conceptions aside to understand. It's what I had to do and it paid off. I</span>
  <span id="freeText18211880477717291749" style="display:none">It was the characters that did it for me.<br /><br />Even though the story was pretty damn brilliant, the characters (who felt like real-life people) were absorbing and moving. I actually can't remember the last time I felt this attached to literary characters.<br /><br />Arav and Jared are complete standouts. The latter will probably be the most controversial and most complex. But go in with an open mind and try to put your personal bias and pre-conceptions aside to understand. It's what I had to do and it paid off. I was both moved and angered but satisfied.<br /><br />The autistic character of Utari is completely adorable and as someone who has an autistic relative with similar comprehension, it hit home in a warm way. There was clearly an effort to delve into her mind. To ask questions about perception and taking in the "ruined" world around her.<br /><br />Regarding the characters on the whole, the depth and detail from each inflexion and mannerism to the words and gestures exchanged are delicate and purposeful. I was there in the discussions and conversations and situations. I was engrossed in it all.<br /><br />Another reviewer mentioned the word 'documentary' and it does feel that way. A drama-doc even. You're a fly on the wall watching it all unfold. You want to touch and intervene but you can't. It's a pretty strange feeling. A good feeling.<br /><br />Definitely worth a second read. It's a huge book but I was determined to finish it. I was hooked.</span>

<div id="review_2735148617" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2735148617" />
    <a title="Steve Cahill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/94280145-steve-cahill"><img alt="Steve Cahill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551965147p2/94280145.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2735148617?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steve Cahill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steve Cahill" href="/user/show/94280145-steve-cahill">Steve Cahill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2735148617" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4972677995762804320">Why can't we have more books like this? Tackles convention and throws the rule book out of the window.<br/><br/>I understand why DOWN AND RISING is dubbed a "hybrid novel". It's not just the creative presentation (reminiscent of Alan Moore's seminal graphic novel, WATCHMEN). It's the feel of the book. It blends an abundace of ingredients for a colourful read.<br/><br/>Now having read this book during a time where we're seeing huge changes in our lifetime, it resonates with me deeply. The bureaucracy and hyprocisy s</span>
  <span id="freeText4972677995762804320" style="display:none">Why can't we have more books like this? Tackles convention and throws the rule book out of the window.<br /><br />I understand why DOWN AND RISING is dubbed a "hybrid novel". It's not just the creative presentation (reminiscent of Alan Moore's seminal graphic novel, WATCHMEN). It's the feel of the book. It blends an abundace of ingredients for a colourful read.<br /><br />Now having read this book during a time where we're seeing huge changes in our lifetime, it resonates with me deeply. The bureaucracy and hyprocisy so prevalent in our government along with the struggles of the average man, woman and child. They are under these microscopes of examination. The why's and how's.<br /><br />I think the feeling I had was a bracing feeling. A fresh take on human observation. Yes, we've seen many a story on the end of the world and how it all goes very bad, very fast. With DOWN AND RISING we get to see this finite period between the aftermath and the next stage of rebuilding. A time capsule I've rarely seen implemented with such focus into a plot.<br /><br />Pro's:<br />Intelligent<br />Incredible character depth<br />Compelling story full of turns, twists and patience<br />Masterful attention to detail<br />Strong messaging - author isn't afraid to go unfiltered<br />Beautiful and emotive artwork<br />Engaging and creative archive material<br /><br />Con's:<br />Heavy book (weight)</span>
  <a data-text-id="4972677995762804320" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2783847113" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2783847113" />
    <a title="Navreet Dhillon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/95968627-navreet-dhillon"><img alt="Navreet Dhillon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555081982p2/95968627.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2783847113?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Navreet Dhillon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Navreet Dhillon" href="/user/show/95968627-navreet-dhillon">Navreet Dhillon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2783847113" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18174264046636204261">This book came highly recommended through my university lecturer. It is the first book I have ever reviewed or have felt compelled to comment on. I'm normally a reader of classics and poetry like Poe and Bronte along with the occassional Stephen King and John le Carré. But I took on the recommedation.<br/><br/>Having read many of the reviews posted by readers, I'm not all too surprised by the praise. From what I understand, this is a debut novel by an indie filmmaker who has clearly demonstrated his writi</span>
  <span id="freeText18174264046636204261" style="display:none">This book came highly recommended through my university lecturer. It is the first book I have ever reviewed or have felt compelled to comment on. I'm normally a reader of classics and poetry like Poe and Bronte along with the occassional Stephen King and John le Carré. But I took on the recommedation.<br /><br />Having read many of the reviews posted by readers, I'm not all too surprised by the praise. From what I understand, this is a debut novel by an indie filmmaker who has clearly demonstrated his writing prowess and confident command over multiple stories and characters.<br /><br />As a British-born Indian, I feel represented just by reading a diverse book where one of the leads is a British-born Indian. It may sound like that is the only reason I'm so invested in this book but it isn't. What drew me in was the focus on human relationships and how important they are especially in the most dire of circumstances. The hardships faced and how a simple connection with another person can empower you to go the extra mile to overcome that hardship.<br /><br />What also spoke to me was the stagnation of society and how they were essentially the footsteps towards complacency, frustration, revolt and violence. It was a message tantamount to our world today. This made many of the moments in reading 'Down and Rising' an eerie read.<br /><br />I felt the strongest moments came when the author was able to wield his pen over the surreal sequences like Gavin's wonderfully haunting dreams and the fiery back and fourth exchanges between the core characters and those in the final chapters (no spoilers) with the antoganists. Exchanges that were blood curdling, angry and passionate.<br /><br />The ending wasn't at all what I expected but saying that, neither was much of the book. It was unpredictable and truly had me on the edge. Great world building and fascinating atmosphere.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18174264046636204261" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2781826021?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas Kelly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas Kelly" href="/user/show/95890866-thomas-kelly">Thomas Kelly</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2781826021" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10522784493606802498">Having been one of the fortunate to watch, and delight in, the highly under rated TV drama series PREMature, I was very much looking forward to reading the directors first venture into prose.<br/><br/>As with his TV scripts, Katbamna’s talent lies in his ability to create real characters, people that we not only feel we know but that we connect with and want to follow them on their journey. As for the story itself, given the state the country is in right now its an almost Nostradamus like prediction of wh</span>
  <span id="freeText10522784493606802498" style="display:none">Having been one of the fortunate to watch, and delight in, the highly under rated TV drama series PREMature, I was very much looking forward to reading the directors first venture into prose.<br /><br />As with his TV scripts, Katbamna’s talent lies in his ability to create real characters, people that we not only feel we know but that we connect with and want to follow them on their journey. As for the story itself, given the state the country is in right now its an almost Nostradamus like prediction of what could happen should we fail to heed the warning signs and continue to point fingers rather than open arms.<br /><br />Be aware this is not an easy read, it challenges you on every front, not least of which is where you stand in human terms. I’m biased because I love his writing but for those that enjoy a fresh approach, the combination of pictures, drawings and other visual material is a first, then do yourself a favour and pick up a copy of this incredible book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10522784493606802498" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2781380236" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2781380236" />
    <a title="Garry Roach" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/95871181-garry-roach"><img alt="Garry Roach" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554889813p2/95871181.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2781380236?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Garry Roach" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Garry Roach" href="/user/show/95871181-garry-roach">Garry Roach</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/95871181-garry-roach?shelf=hybrid">hybrid</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/95871181-garry-roach?shelf=mindfulness">mindfulness</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2781380236" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3280075192547116123">This came recommended through a friend at work due to my interest in psychology and strangely because of my love for classic Japanese cinema. Now let me explain the reasoning for the Japanese cinema reference. My viewing library consists of films by Akira Kurosawa, Masaki Kobayashi, Yoji Yamada, Kenji Mizoguchi and Yasujirō Ozu. All directors who specialised in themes on humanity and purpose in life. I've always been fascinated by this and felt alot of my teen years and 20's were shaped by these</span>
  <span id="freeText3280075192547116123" style="display:none">This came recommended through a friend at work due to my interest in psychology and strangely because of my love for classic Japanese cinema. Now let me explain the reasoning for the Japanese cinema reference. My viewing library consists of films by Akira Kurosawa, Masaki Kobayashi, Yoji Yamada, Kenji Mizoguchi and Yasujirō Ozu. All directors who specialised in themes on humanity and purpose in life. I've always been fascinated by this and felt alot of my teen years and 20's were shaped by these films and their messages.<br /><br />With that preface I come to Down and Rising - Six Days in a Ruined World. From the outset it's all about the people in this story. The principal players and their own missions of preservation and search for meaning/truth. Throughout my read I came to find a transformation of character stories flowing in waves of emotion and action all with an intention to emphasize the human condition. The why's and how's of their decisions and the psychological makeup (in many cases, the changing makeup).<br /><br />As casual comic reader I found the artwork to be on par with some of the most emotive I've seen. The decision to present the main characters in nude was quite beautiful and tasteful. Having black ink on white paper made it quite elegant.<br /><br />Referencing back to classic Japanese cinema I want to mention the violence element. In both the book and the aforementioned cinema genre there is control to the violence. It doesn't read like a cheap thrill or tasteless. There is profound purpose to each act of brutality and it is just as important to the forward motion of the overall story and character development.<br /><br />Last thing. The bonus material is highly creative and truly digs deeper into not only the creative decisions on the author and illustrator's parts but also provides insights into the effort to involve the reader by crossing over from observer to participant particularly with the reader's notes pages between chapters.<br /><br />5 stars without a doubt.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3280075192547116123" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

But it is not to say that it dampened my experience. <br/><br/>Perhaps a second read will have me acclimated to this level of intensity.<br/><br/>A special mention should go to the attentive detail so dearly appreciated and the splendid artwork.<br/><br/>I think with time, 'Down and Rising' will age like a fine wine.</span>

<div id="review_2771355575" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2771355575" />
    <a title="Kyle Lynch" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/95519715-kyle-lynch"><img alt="Kyle Lynch" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554144497p2/95519715.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2771355575?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kyle Lynch" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kyle Lynch" href="/user/show/95519715-kyle-lynch">Kyle Lynch</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2771355575" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7265739351459164995">This is an exceptional work with realistic dialogue.<br/><br/>The latter made this an engrossing read. The exchanges between characters in high-tension situations were matched by the subtle pauses and powerful silences in the quieter moments.<br/><br/>I truly appreciated the focus on how Arav's love for his daughter was sewn throughout the entirety of the story. How it was never forgotten and empowered every action and word. It made the ending so profound.<br/><br/>Sofia was a rarity in the sense that the typical 'good-looki</span>
  <span id="freeText7265739351459164995" style="display:none">This is an exceptional work with realistic dialogue.<br /><br />The latter made this an engrossing read. The exchanges between characters in high-tension situations were matched by the subtle pauses and powerful silences in the quieter moments.<br /><br />I truly appreciated the focus on how Arav's love for his daughter was sewn throughout the entirety of the story. How it was never forgotten and empowered every action and word. It made the ending so profound.<br /><br />Sofia was a rarity in the sense that the typical 'good-looking woman' was written with such depth and tragedy. Her story was an immigrant's tale covered in the ashes of the apocalypse.<br /><br />As much of a standout as every character was, Jared Thomas was the most frighteningly real. He seemed to me to be the bravest character to create and form. His exchanges with Layla were heartbreaking at times, considering the circumstances. But at the same time, there was such a mighty connection that seemed unspoken.<br /><br />Saying that, much of Down and Rising had an unspoken component to it. An undergrowth of second meanings and deeper messaging.<br /><br />What's actually strange is that many of the newspaper cuttings featured in the book have a 'from the future' feel. Quite freaky. I suppose that was the intention.<br /><br />As a photographer, I admired the use of the artform interlaced throughout the archive pages. The face-off between Darlington and Lawrence is a standout. I can see these images on city billboards across England.<br /><br />I highly recommend this "hybrid novel" for its daring nature and originality.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7265739351459164995" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      Element.show('savingMessage')

    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('oSFiU8M6BR3lBaXi8D4SAN8DA3FlRZ0ozpre8OabB/d88h7FixF/lpq5oAtkFiju4bCe39HGuVgXw8pw98Sk1g==')})
  }

</script>

creed of millions of ordinary Americans.A brilliant analysis-and funny to boot-What\'s the Matter with Kansas? is a vivid portrait of an upside-down world where blue-collar patriots recite the Pledge Drawing on years of research and first-hand reporting, Frank points out that the Democrats have done little to advance traditional liberal goals: expanding opportunity, fighting for social justice, and ensuring that workers get a fair deal. Indeed, they have scarcely dented the free-market consensus at all. This is not for lack of opportunity: Democrats have occupied the White House for sixteen of the last twenty-four years, and yet the decline of the middle class has only accelerated. Wall Street gets its bailouts, wages keep falling, and the free-trade deals keep coming.\n\nWith his trademark sardonic wit and lacerating logic, Frank\'s Listen, Liberal lays bare the essence of the Democratic Party\'s philosophy and how it has changed over the years. A form of corporate and cultural elitism has largely eclipsed the party\'s old working-class commitment, he finds. For certain favored groups, this has meant prosperity. But for the nation as a whole, it is a one-way ticket into the abyss of inequality. In this critical election year, Frank recalls the Democrats to their historic goals-the only way to reverse the ever-deepening rift between the rich and the poor in America.<\/span>\n  <a It permits us, through it<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText8323231118568266545\" style=\"display:none\">The liberal class plays a vital role in a democracy. It gives moral legitimacy to the state. It makes limited forms of dissent and incremental change possible. The liberal class posits itself as the conscience of the nation. It permits us, through its appeal to public virtues and the public good, to define ourselves as a good and noble people. Most importantly, on behalf of the power elite the liberal class serves as bulwarks against radical movements by offering a safety valve for popular frustrations and discontentment by discrediting those who talk of profound structural change. Once this class loses its social and political role then the delicate fabric of a democracy breaks down and the liberal class, along with the values it espouses, becomes an object of ridicule and hatred. The door that has been opened to proto-fascists has been opened by a bankrupt liberalism  The Death of the Liberal Class examines the failure of the liberal class to confront the rise of the corporate state and the consequences of a liberalism that has become profoundly bankrupted. Hedges argues there are five pillars of the liberal establishment – the press, liberal religious institutions, labor unions, universities and the Democratic Party— and that each of these institutions, more concerned with status and privilege than justice and progress, sold out the constituents they represented. In doing so, the liberal class has become irrelevant to society at large and ultimately the corporate power elite they once served.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"8323231118568266545\" href=\"#\" Butler was a military hero of the first rank, the winner of two Medals of Honour, a true \'fighting marine\' whose courage and patriotism could not be doubted. Yet he came to believe that the wars in which he and his men had fought and bled and died were all pre-planned conflicts, designed not so much to defend America as to bloat the balance sheets of US banks and corporations.\n\nWar Is a Racket is the title of two works, a speech and a booklet, by retired United States Marine Corps Major General and two time Medal of Honor recipient Smedley D. Butler. In them, Butler frankly discusses from his experience as a career military officer how business interests commercially benefit from warfare.\n\nAfter his retirement from the Marine Corps, Gen. Butler made a nationwide tour in the early 1930s giving his speech &quot;War is a Racket&quot;. The speech was so well received that he wrote a longer version as a small book with the same title that was published in 1935 by Round Table Press, Inc., of New York. The booklet was also condensed in Reader\'s Digest as a book supplement which helped popularize his message. In an introduction to the Reader\'s Digest version, Lowell Thomas, the &quot;as told to&quot; author of Butler\'s oral autobiographical adventures, praised Butler\'s &quot;moral as well as physical <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16810354036460565640">Born in Hammersmith, England, Rohith S. Katbamna began his writing career in the film and television industry.<br/><br/>Following on from his work with the BBC, Channel 4 and IFC, including his acclaimed documentary, Hooking in JoBurg, Rohith’s feature debut came at the age of 28 when he wrote, produced, shot and directed the British television miniseries, PREMature. A culmination of a decade of work on the</span>
  <span id="freeText16810354036460565640" style="display:none">Born in Hammersmith, England, Rohith S. Katbamna began his writing career in the film and television industry.<br /><br />Following on from his work with the BBC, Channel 4 and IFC, including his acclaimed documentary, Hooking in JoBurg, Rohith’s feature debut came at the age of 28 when he wrote, produced, shot and directed the British television miniseries, PREMature. A culmination of a decade of work on the professional circuit.<br /><br />With the success of the series, he dedicated the next three years towards honing his writing craft through his debut hybrid novel.<br /><br />On Down and Rising: "It's a response to social and political tensions, with an emphasis on humanistic themes and psychological drama."</span>
